<user_id>114205011930121959876</user_id><name>Joe Mullin<//name>< date>
1578532615379< /date>
< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< Text>
Nice staff, clean place, good prices, free carts to use, bathrooms to use, convenient location, but has a couple interesting quirks.  Public Storage took this place over a while back and are making it better, but there are some interesting quirks they're still working on from the previous owners, like upgrading all the lighting and updating the storage unit doors.  Note that the storage doors require a cylinder lock, you can't use a normal disc lock.  Cylinder locks are more secure - no one is breaking in there - they sell the cylinder locks at a normal online price (from what I could find).  Overall, their prices for the units and their supplies all seem quite reasonable.

Unit prices "off the street" are pretty high like everything else in the valley, but if you do the online or call-in reservation, they have very good prices and deals.  I had called the Public Storage "call center" and they kind of rush you into getting a reservation, but don't be afraid to tell them to slow down and tell you about all the options.  I got a price cheaper than what they showed on their website.  After I got a reservation, I made an appointment to come in and check it out the same day.  I then said I'd come back in a week to do the paperwork because I didn't want to start renting for another week - the reservation just guarantees you the size for the price as long as the size is available.  So, if they are low on stock for what you want, don't wait to rent.  When I came back a week later, Gerardo helped me, he is very nice and knowledgeable.  We toured the unit, noticed the light bulb was burnt out, signed the paperwork, and he then went and replaced the light bulb in my unit.  All the paperwork is digital and modern (yay!).  I got the unit I wanted for the price I was promised a week ago.  Thanks!< /Text>

<gmap_id>0x80dcae440dd1140f:0x145226c36298e65b</gmap_id><Date>1543377959747< /Date>< Review>
I'm partial to simple, American pub-style food, and this is one of my favorite places to get it near UCR. I usually get their burgers or pizzas, which are greasy but tasty and generously-portioned, but I haven't been disappointed by anything of theirs I've tried yet. The atmosphere is relaxed and usually not too crowded, and the staff gives you your space but is perfectly friendly and willing to help if you need anything. There's usually not too long a wait for the food, and it's open conveniently late if you're a night owl. As long as you go in expecting pub fare and not fine dining, I don't think you'll be disappointed.< /Review>

Jason Lum<//Name>
<Time>1458232218583< /Time>< rate>
5<//rate>
<Text>Aw Yeah GETAWAY!!!! For the locals it's pronounced "Ghetto-way Cafe". I don't know where to beginning. You stole my heart, you had me at hello. Before I start my review, I would like to address a few of the negative reviews. Now I understand 3 star reviews, this place is not the best for everyone, but anything lower.. I don't know what you are smoking. Take that stick out of your A$S and take your "I've had better" attitude and just leave. We don't need your kind at Getaway anyway. If you don't drink beer, what-the-f**k are you doing here? You don't see me going to a Vegan restaurant and giving it 1 star, because there's no meat. If you are only willing to eat Costco Pizza or some crappy Domino's because of how cheap you are, just leave. Deuces!

Getaway has very reasonably priced entrees and has great portions. Its hard to truly describe this place without you actually going here. The food is kind of like a ghetto gourmet. It's not fast food or Denny's, but it's got a very light sprinkle of gourmet to it. Your best bet is to go with the Burgers. They are not out of this world, but still delicious. Take it from a picky burger eater, they get the job done. Also, the sandwiches are all pretty good. The pizza is a tricky one, some are either good or nasty. It really depends on which favor you choose. I'd say go for the basic meat varieties and play it safe.

To truly appreciate Getaway you must be UCR student or Alumni or at least live in Riverside. Or else you wouldn't understand, it's Riverside thing. Maybe that saying will stick... its better than hearing someone say "it's a Jersey thing". No offense to Ghetto-siders, UCR is freaking the bomb dot com. Great people, great parties, great b**.. I mean ladies, and Great Engineer, Business school (now/soon a Med school and Law school, so suck it other UC's that don't have either) besides going to UCR, RIVERSIDE F***ing sucks! I lived there for a little while after graduating and I was slowly rotting away in the Inland-SMOG Empire. Ghetto-way is your only Getaway!

From the outside.. there isn't much to see. In fact the first time I met a friend here, I wasn't sure if this place was part of the apartments directly behind it. I walked in to what appeared to be a side door, but is really the front door. It was completely dark and only lit by neon glow of sport and beer signs. I almost walked out, because I thought there's no way I will like this place. I was just barely under the drinking age (haha like it matters in college) and hated the taste of beer, but something about this bar smell of wood and beer, and the taste of a decent burger made me feel at peace. Also, a few quarters can buy you a game on a very horrible, but fun pool table. Even before I would learn to give up fruit drinks and have a love for great tasting beers, there was something about Getaway that just felt like home...

I most likely will never be caught dead in Riverside with the exception of catching up with friends, but I miss my favorite beer. DROP TOP!! Try it! Stupid Yard House has it listed on their site, but nearly every YH I went to in socal does not serve it. If you are a UCR student, you must try this place at least once. Bring your buddies and relax and don't take life too seriously. If you are looking for something unbelievable and with white table clothes, don't bother. If you like decently priced beer and kick back atmosphere. It's Getaway time for you.

**I have no idea why I'm writing a review at 3:30 AM on a weekday, but I felt I need to give back to Getaway. I am grateful for all the good times. Thank you Thank you. Until we meet again. For now if my buddies are reading this, please poor some Drop Top off to the side for me. **</Text>< Pics>

<Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
While I wish the buses ran on Sundays and later into the evenings. The system is set up in a way that seems to cater to the Yuba City area most while Marysville busses are an hourly loop as opposed to the half in neighboring Sutter County.
I will tell you there is a good fleet of drivers shuttling around our community members mostly consisting of disabled and low-income individuals who depend on this system to take them where they need to go be it loop bus, dial a ride or commuter routes.
The busses are clean and I know should someone puke or seriously soil the bus the driver will promptly swap out busses allowing us to enjoy clean and sanitary busses.
We have encountered a few drivers that I am astonished still drive with the way they treat riders. The dark haired man with a complexion that would perhaps be of Hispanic or Italian decent is worth a mention for he could use a lesson in kindness and compassion. There is also a guy that drives me to Lynda many mornings during the work week who is consistently kind and considerate to riders I see boarding and unloading. Jane is another driver who is well trained and knowledgeable about the bus system.
The new shelters put in place a few months ago were a much needed to shelter us from the elements and despite countless attempts by deadbeats at trashing the shelters we all enjoy it is good to see they are maintained daily.
Finally, I wish there were more bus tickets given out to the poor people of our community. Bus passes are a resource far and too few in between.<//Text>

<Review>What can one say? Safeway is Safeway! This one is not especially better or worse than any other Safeway. It has all the usual items we expect Safeway to have. You will find lots of cans and cereals and paper towels and tomato sauces. It has the usual baked goods, cheese selection, and butcher. What does distinguish this Safeway for many others I have visited is the small plaza they built at a time when lots of people could gather in a socially not very distant way. Today there are no chairs just a few tables that are cemented to the floor. However, being able to sit in the plaza and watch people go bye really makes sheltering in place a lot easier. So thanks Safeway for thinking of the community when you designed this store!< /Review>< Response>

< Review>
For the past 6 months since the Covid lockdown, ive yet to witness this Safeway being low in stock of anything. Not to mention a few well lit areas to lockup your bike safely is🙌🏾key! The staff and security is always friendly and helpful. Their prices can be a lil higher than most grocery stores is my discovery. For those items I simply purchase in bulk or online. For the chef and baker in me, I find what I need to make small batch baked goods and meal planning. Look out weekly for managers specials and buy one get one free items. It actually pays to use the coupons and digital member numbers for extra discounts. Every penny counts these days. One thing this Safeway will not run out of is Baby Grape Tomatoes.... Oy vey!</Review>

No matter the time of day, this store is a pain.
* Always a line with a more than necessary wait
* Inattentive staff
* Shelves always feel low or out of stock
* No cell signal in store
* Self checkout machines are the absolute WORST and attendant non-existent
* Express line rarely open

Prices are mediocre for a frustrating experience. I shop here as little as possible.

Shelter in Place Update:
* They stopped offering sanitation wipes
* Restocking is abysmal
* Clearly trying to cut costs with minimal concern for staff

Please take some cues from Trader Joe’s who are doing a much better job.<//review>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
Of of the only places open 24/7 near Berkeley for groceries or other products! Make sure to walk left from the elevator if going late at night, as the first entrance from the elevator is closed at night, but don’t mistake the entire Safeway as closed! Being one of the few places open at all hours everyday of the week near Berkeley or Oakland, I’ve only been here very late at night once my closer preferred community Safeway has already closed.

They have great little hidden parking lot that is up from College ave, and also has an entrance on Claremont I believe. I was shocked at first to first such a big parking lot nestled above college ave shops, as you would never guess a huge parking lot would be on such a busy part of a Main Street, but it is hidden on the second floor! So the parking is super convenient and then you can either take an elevator or the stores down to the first floor where the entrance to the store is!< /text>

< text>
It's a Safeway, so it's a mixed bag. They have enough of the important things, and the hours are certainly convenient.

It's not the worse Safeway ever, but it's not the best.

Still, it's really a pedestrian area.

It's a bit of an eyesore, and it blocks the view of the hills.

And having a big supermarket here makes the traffic even worse than it was.

The parking lot is often full, which means the streets nearby get clogged with people trying to parallel park.

It would have been so nice to have had a park here.< /text>

< review>
On the bright side, it’s a store in the neighborhood and have a lot of stuff in sales - whatever you need - it’s there, and with the new management the long lines and the dreadful waiting is slowly dying out. The workers are all professional and there to assist you. But, on the other side, if there was another pharmacy near my home, I would rather go there.  Why? Well, the employees might be pleasant, but they are often not following their word, so the waiting is long. I could have been dead million times by far if my life depended on waiting for them. It takes time to process meds and go through their system. Now, that not might be in their power, but it is certainly a downfall for this pharmacy. They often lack meds in stock - not all, but some that  I need.</review>

Smaller than other Safeway stores and the layout is a bit funky too - so it took me a bit of time to get oriented. They also didn’t have nearly the variety of products that larger stores have.  For example, the yogurt aisle/area at most Safeways has maybe 50-100 different varieties - the one here had maybe 10-15?  Yes, it’s a minor qualm, but when you get used to shopping at a larger store, you set your expectations at a certain level and I ended up disappointed after shopping there.  On the plus side, there’s plenty of parking (on top of the store) and the seating area outside in the small plaza with Philz, Supercuts, etc. is reasonably pleasant.<//review>
